  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fb03028c-15f6-4e23-910d-e0589348ed2d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer11683726327984807268">The world has suffered a magic apocalypse. We pushed the technological progress too far, and now magic returned with a vengeance.   <span id="freeText11683726327984807268" style="display:none">The world has suffered a magic apocalypse. We pushed the technological progress too far, and now magic returned with a vengeance. It comes in waves, without warning, and vanishes as suddenly as it appears. When magic is up, planes drop out of the sky, cars stall, electricity dies. When magic is down, guns work and spells fail.<br /><br />Atlanta would be a nice place to live, if it weren’t for magic… One moment magic dominates, and cars stall and guns fail. The next, technology takes over and the defensive spells no longer protect your house from monsters. Here skyscrapers topple under onslaught of magic; werebears and werehyenas prowl through the ruined streets; and the Masters of the Dead, necromancers driven by their thirst of knowledge and wealth, pilot blood-crazed vampires with their minds. In this world lives Kate Daniels. Kate likes her sword a little too much and has a hard time controlling her mouth. The magic in her blood makes her a target, and she spent most of her life hiding in plain sight. But when Kate’s guardian is murdered, she must choose to do nothing and remain safe or to pursue his preternatural killer. Hiding is easy, but the right choice is rarely easy…</span>
  <a data-text-id="11683726327984807268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/158473-i-m-rereading-the-series-just-to-get-ready"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm rereading the series just to get ready for the recent addition and I came across something that bothered me or I couldn't figure out....Why did everyone place the blame on Kate suspecting Crest of being the upir when it was Curran/Jim/etc who liked him as a suspect and put words in her mouth? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7933543-gnome-claire-wishes-she-was-as-cool-as-gnome-ann"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1473246053i/7933543._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7933543-gnome-claire-wishes-she-was-as-cool-as-gnome-ann">Gnome Claire *Wishes she was as cool as Gnome Ann*</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Someone suggested that the hunch he is blaming her for is the upir theory (which was right Curran!), but her theory wasn't the reason that they all tu<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Someone suggested that the hunch he is blaming her for is the upir theory (which was right Curran!), but her theory wasn't the reason that they all turned up at Crest's door, that was down to Curran and Jim.<br /><br />She seemed to go along with it on on the basis that she didn't know Crest well enough to rule him (which was true- they pointed out to her that she couldn't rule him out) out but seemed a bit shocked by the idea he might be a cannibalistic serial killer (as you would be) and had a little freak out moment when she thought she might be dating the upir, she never said she thought he was but you'd still freak out at the possibility. <br /><br />While a normal person might want to jump to the conclusion they definitely weren't dating a monster in Kate's dangerous world that would be a odd assumption, she's hiding her heritage so she know that others would be hiding theirs too. She didn't rule him out but she didn't agree either. I thought the way that Curran treated her there was really unfair.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9070092722866312210"><b>3.5 stars<br/><br/>10 Reasons to Love Kate Daniels:</b><br/><br/>1. She doesn't take any crap from anyone.<br/>2. She's sarcastic and occasionally rude and always hilarious. Who else would greet a snarly Beast Lord with "Here, kitty, kitty...?"<br/>3. She knows all the rules of diplomacy when dealing with shapeshifters, vampires, and other supernaturals.<br/>4. She knows how to <i>break</i> all those rules and commands respect in spite of it.<br/>5. She admits when she makes mistakes.<br/>6. She's comfortable with herself and who she is. But she's lo</span>
  <span id="freeText9070092722866312210" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars<br /><br />10 Reasons to Love Kate Daniels:</b><br /><br />1. She doesn't take any crap from anyone.<br />2. She's sarcastic and occasionally rude and always hilarious. Who else would greet a snarly Beast Lord with "Here, kitty, kitty...?"<br />3. She knows all the rules of diplomacy when dealing with shapeshifters, vampires, and other supernaturals.<br />4. She knows how to <i>break</i> all those rules and commands respect in spite of it.<br />5. She admits when she makes mistakes.<br />6. She's comfortable with herself and who she is. But she's lonely too, and she isn't afraid to acknowledge it.<br />7. She has a lot of men in her life that she likes for different reasons. But she won't hesitate to call them out if she thinks they're crossing the line.<br />8. She has a huge amount of decency and integrity. Exhausted, hurt, bleeding, and hungry, she'll still stop eating when she thinks someone else is being slighted.<br />9. She wields a mean sword that she calls "Slayer" that she uses to kill all kinds of vicious creatures.<br />10. She kicks <i>serious</i> ass, with or without magic.<br /><br />I have a hit-or-miss track record with most urban fantasy books that I've tried, but I think Kate and I are going to get along just fine. Can't wait to read the next book! And the one after that, and the one after that...<br /></span>

<div id="review_351655149" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351655149" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351655149?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7940930-magic-bites">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">The WHOLE world. Also--world-building questions answered here.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=weres-shapeshifters">weres-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351655149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3772412201484514518"><b>5/5/18:</b> Still love it (if that wasn’t evident by virtue of having read it SIX times). If you haven’t read this, you should. Immediately. 📚🖤<br/><br/>This is my F-A-V-O-R-I-T-E series. <br/><br/>And that's kind of a big deal. For example, if you asked me what my second favorite series was, I'd have to give you a top 5 list. BUT. KATE DANIELS is unquestionably my #1 favorite. <br/><br/>I'm rereading the series, b/c the new book is out next Tuesday, and I think this is my fifth (or sixth?) time. I typically can't reread a serie</span>
  <span id="freeText3772412201484514518" style="display:none"><b>5/5/18:</b> Still love it (if that wasn’t evident by virtue of having read it SIX times). If you haven’t read this, you should. Immediately. 📚🖤<br><br>This is my F-A-V-O-R-I-T-E series. <br><br>And that's kind of a big deal. For example, if you asked me what my second favorite series was, I'd have to give you a top 5 list. BUT. KATE DANIELS is unquestionably my #1 favorite. <br><br>I'm rereading the series, b/c the new book is out next Tuesday, and I think this is my fifth (or sixth?) time. I typically can't reread a series every year b/c I get bored, and I thought that might be a problem this time, but, NOPE, it's not.<br><br>This is also the series I immediately suggest when asked for a reading recommendation, and it's hooked every person that's taken that advice. When I'm harassing people for feedback, they've all liked MAGIC BITES enough to read the next book, which is good b/c unlike most series, this one just keeps getting better. <br><br><b>There have, however, been a few complaints that this first book is a little confusing on the world-building front</b>. I can't be completely objective, b/c looking back after reading the series five(+) times . . . hindsight is, after all, 20/20.<br><br>The basic premise is brand new: the world began with magic and technology existing in a harmonious balance. <br><br>The analogy made is of a pendulum swinging only slightly back (magic) and forth (technology). But over time man developed magic, causing the pendulum to swing increasingly wildly until the pendulum crashed to the other side, leaving only a minimal amount of magic behind and flooding the world with the ability to use technology in magic's stead. <br><br>I pictured it like that boat ride at theme parks--at Carowinds it's called the Frenzoid--that starts out swinging slowing back and forth, gaining momentum, until finally, after a nerve-wracking several seconds held completely upside down, it crashes to the other side. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405507186i/10407543.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This happens approximately every 4000(ish) years, most recently about 40 years prior to the present time in the book. <br><br>The changeover from magic-to-tech, or in the book's case, tech-to-magic, is not immediately complete. Like the Frenzoid, after the initial shift from back-and-forth to completing a full circle, the momentum keeps the boat (or magic/tech) swinging wildly back and forth until it settles down in the middle, or <i>magic</i> in MAGIC BITES. <br><br>As man develops magic to replace the lost technology, the process begins again, and in another 4000ish years the reverse shift will occur.<br><br>I honestly can't remember how well this is explained in book 1, but I <i>do</i> know that if it <i>wasn't</i> fully explained, <b>I did not care.</b> It was secondary to the plot and the characters. <br><br>I knew that sometimes magic worked and sometimes it didn't. Same for technology. I knew that when magic worked, guns wouldn't fire, and that spells didn't work when tech was up. <br><br>I also knew this was why Kate carried a sword--b/c a sword <i>always</i> works.&lt;-----Kate is KICK-ASS.<br><br>And that was enough information for me, b/c who cares about world-building when you have a main character like Kate Daniels? <br><br>Not me. <br><br>Kate is the perfect heroine. On the surface, she's the standard Urban Fantasy MC: she's super special magically and snarktastic. Oftentimes this can get old, but not Kate Daniels, who after numerous rereads only gets more fantastic. <br><br>Unlike other UF heroines, Kate's brand of special kept her <i>truly</i> isolated. She didn't <i>feel</i> alone, she <i>was</i> alone. Anything else meant death. And yeah, her mouth is always getting her into trouble, but Kate often reveals her vulnerability right before she attacks:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Curran turned to me. "Take one of mine again and I'll kill you." He said it in a conversational manner, matter-of-fact and flat, but in his eyes I could see a simple certainty. If he had to, he would kill me. He would not lose any sleep over it. He would not give it a second thought. He would do it and move on, untroubled by ending my existence.<br><b>It scared the shit out of me, so I laughed in his face</b>.</i>
</blockquote><br>She was scared. So she laughed. In his FACE. <br><br>And <i>that</i>, ladies and gentlemen, is why I love Kate. <br><br>She doesn't bitch and moan about how life isn't fair, why her? She does what needs doing, and she often does it hilariously. <br><br>She's my favorite.<br><br>Teenage girls everywhere wish that they were Katniss Everdeen. I wish I was Kate Daniels.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393429087ra/8710692.gif" width="480" height="251" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136352204" rel="nofollow noopener">A Questionable Client (Kate Daniels, #0.5)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351650230" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns (Kate Daniels, #2)</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114648463?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer114648463&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114648463" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12863199179529059657">Ever ventured out into the world of dating and discovered that it was disproportionately populated with assholes? Did you ever look around and say, "Where the hell are all these assholes coming from?"<br/><br/>Well, if Curran turned your oven on then the answer is possibly: You!<br/><br/>Yes, that's right. Assholes who have the common traits of narcissism, marchiavellianism and pyscopathy according to recent studies, score more with the ladies. It's called the Dark Triad (I know - best name ever) and in many respec</span>
  <span id="freeText12863199179529059657" style="display:none">Ever ventured out into the world of dating and discovered that it was disproportionately populated with assholes? Did you ever look around and say, "Where the hell are all these assholes coming from?"<br /><br />Well, if Curran turned your oven on then the answer is possibly: You!<br /><br />Yes, that's right. Assholes who have the common traits of narcissism, marchiavellianism and pyscopathy according to recent studies, score more with the ladies. It's called the Dark Triad (I know - best name ever) and in many respects these aspects of a person can be considered partially genetic traits. So when ladies hook up with the dirtbags, they occassionally spawn a entirely new generation to fill up a gene pool that obviously NEEDS more jerks.<br /><br />I'm not going to bag out Magic Bites because I actually really, really enjoyed it. I'm looking forward to reading the next book in the series, which I'm about to start, but either Curran needs to have a major personality overhaul or he needs to be boinking someone else. He's aggressive, petty, arrogant, dismissive and violent. And yes, I caught myself thinking he was hot on a couple of occasions.<br /><br />I will submit myself for regular beatings - with nunchucks later. Nunchucks can cure anything.<br /><br />I really loved the concept, I loved the world and its interesting take on vampires and the governing associations that run the world. I had just a LITTLE bit of a problem with the characterization. <br /><br />Okay, I might get crucified for this, but Kate Daniels actually really reminded me of Anita Blake. <br /><br />Paranormal mystery solver? Check!<br />Daggy clothes and utter disregard to style? Check!<br />Tough-talking super bravado? Check!<br />Solves everything with violence or an over abundance of natural magical ability? Check!<br /><br />Obviously when more than two men had an overly enthusiastic sexual interest in Kate, my Pavlovian conditioning kicked in and I was half prepared for Kate Daniels to turn into a slutqueen with a magical vagina. You have no idea how happy I was when she didn't!<br /><br />I did like her better than Anita though as she had moments of maturity when she decided that tough talk and threats of violence weren't really conducive to what she needed and thus backed down and recognized that she can't defeat evil with her badassery alone (Anita will never discover this because even if she died, she'd just seduce God and steal his powers and then we'd ALL be in a lot of trouble!)<br /><br />Also, when the chips were down, she got drunk, sat on her porch and DARED the world to come and get her. I like it. Best. Fucking. Plan. Ever. I felt true sisterly affection for her then!<br /><br />The mystery was painfully easy but I dismissed that because everything else was covered in so much badass awesomeness. Besides, right from the start, Kate laid out her very tactical sleuthing plan and I immediately knew that she was definitely NOT Poirot or Sherlock Holmes. She was SUPPOSED to be bad at it and thus she gets my seal of approval. It's truly aweinspiring when you can suck arse at something and still come out on top! I love it.<br /><br />So, over all, THOUGH I only gave it three stars, I actually liked it. Funny, fun, a little bit sexy and a good, light read.<br /><br />Except for all the gruesome death, rape, stabbing, decomposing and dying.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12863199179529059657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_50496487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50496487" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50496487?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of gritty urban fantasy and occult detective fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=magic-noir">magic-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=kickbutt-heroine">kickbutt-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-adore">heroine-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=slavic-folklore">slavic-folklore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=mage">mage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2020-action-heroines-yearly-challen">2020-action-heroines-yearly-challen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50496487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17649825650272456168"><b> Completed an audiobook reread of this book in July. Here are my thoughts on this reread. Most of the meat on the bones is in my first review.<br/><br/>I am glad I reread this. It was a great book, but I forgot quite a bit of what happened. It's pretty edgy even today. A hefty dose of the horrific in the type of villain it features and the highly heinous deeds he commits. Kate Daniels is badass. She is snarky, but has the ability to back it up. I enjoyed her dialogue and I appreciated being inside her hea</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17649825650272456168" style="display:none"><b> Completed an audiobook reread of this book in July. Here are my thoughts on this reread. Most of the meat on the bones is in my first review.<br /><br />I am glad I reread this. It was a great book, but I forgot quite a bit of what happened. It's pretty edgy even today. A hefty dose of the horrific in the type of villain it features and the highly heinous deeds he commits. Kate Daniels is badass. She is snarky, but has the ability to back it up. I enjoyed her dialogue and I appreciated being inside her head and seeing the world through her eyes. For an urban fantasy, this book is highly dystopian. A near future setting where Atlanta is devastated by a magical cataclysm. In the time of COVID-19, it seems very prescient. <br /><br />I liked the 'flirting' with Curran, if you want to call it that. I appreciate that Kate doesn't compromise who she is just because he's the Beast Lord. And he's very scary, tbh. I really like Derek as Kate's sidekick. <br /><br />Renee Raudman is a very good narrator. She has a great way of making Kate sound lethal but also deliver's her snarky lines perfectly. She's also good at male voices as well. <br /><br />I would recommend checking out this Audiobook, even if you're read this before.</b><br />****************<br /><br /><br />About twelve years ago, there was a little girl named Danielle who read a book called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7025629.Guilty_Pleasures__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___1_" title="Guilty Pleasures (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #1) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Guilty Pleasures</a> by Laurell K. Hamilton, and was seduced into the dark, enchanting world of urban fantasy. She went on to read more urban fantasy than she could shake a stick at. Over the years, she lost touch with Anita Blake, and mourned the loss of a tough-as-nails, kickass, urban fantasy heroine to join for exciting, dangerous, and magical adventures. <br /><br />Recently, she finally picked up a book called Magic Bites, which had been sitting on her bloated, embarrassingly large tbr pile. She read it to find out who this mysterious "Beast Lord" was, and why everyone thought that Kate and Curran were the best urban fantasy couple. That young girl is a very happy camper.<br /><br />Magic Bites is a hard book to describe. If you are a genuine, die-hard urban fantasy fan, you will like this book. At 260 pages, it appears deceptively slim. However, there's a lot of information, adventure, description, and incredibly good writing in that relatively small amount of pages. I will admit that this book made being confused and baffled fun for me. I had a lot of questions as I was reading. Still do. But that's kind of nice. <br /><br />Kate Daniels is one of the best urban fantasy heroines I've had the pleasure to meet. I've said before that I don't care for arrogant, braggadocious, posturing characters. She doesn't posture. She simply is a bad-ass, but down to earth, at the same time. She doesn't run around in bustiers, low-riding leather pants, and stiletto heels, climbing out of bed with some random guy long enough to kick-butt. She wears clothes that facilitate her ability to kick ass and to keep herself alive. Being cute is all good and well, but in her world, being cute might get her killed. Her only vanity is her long hair, which she keeps in a braid most of the time. Lethal abilities aside, Kate is very feminine. She can appreciate a cute guy, and she had flaws and weaknesses just like the rest of us armchair kickbutt heroines. I like her no-nonsense view of the world, her snarky sense of humor, and the fact that she likes to pull the lion by the tail, sometimes literally. I thought she was an interesting character. She has some emotional wounds that she is dealing with, and tends to keep her own company. It's nice to see a thoughtful, almost brooding heroine in this genre.<br /><br />Ms. Andrews earned my respect. The Atlanta that she has created is a very fascinating place. I still don't understand all of what occurred to make Atlanta very much like a dystopic wastleland, but I didn't have to understand that to enjoy this book. I do know that magic plays a huge hand in the catastrophe that hit this fair Southern city. It seems to surge and ebb, like the electricity brownouts that were hitting California when I lived out there. For all the importance that magic plays in this story, Ms. Andrews is never heavy-handed with the use of magic. In fact, she lightly and skillfully builds a storyline that is credible and interesting around the tendrils of magic power wielded in different ways by many of the characters in this novel. And better yet, she was able to create a female magic-wielder who wasn't a witch. I believe there are far too many witch urban fantasy and paranormal heroines. It's gotten to the point where it's almost cliche'. Her use of folklore is clever and well-placed. She takes a different direction with vampires, shapechangers, and mages. I must say I've never seen vampires described in the manner in which they exist in this story. They are quite gruesome and almost pitiful in Kate Daniels' world. <br /><br />I have to say that Ilona Andrews writing is high class. She sets the scenes very well, using language in just the right way, to keep the story flowing forward. She employs the noir elements that I enjoy in urban fantasy and occult detective novels very well. Better yet, she treats the reader with respect, understanding that popular fiction readers like to be challenged and fully engaged. She seems to understand that just because we enjoy fantastic, escapist material, it doesn't mean that we want to read something meaningless and without substance. In fact, I felt as though I was reading a police procedural with magical and horrific elements (a sure sign of a good occult detective novel). I thought I had figured out who the killer was fairly early on (and was about to be disappointed), but I was way off. When the reveal happens, it comes at you in such a manner that you cannot help but admire how skillfully the red herring and clues were laid out. <br /><br />As I read this book, my brain, which always tries to make order and sense of things, tried to think of a way to categorize and classify this book and the world within it. I never came up with a concrete classification. But that's a good thing. It's nice to find something new within a well-loved genre, and to encounter a novel reading experience at the same time. This book delivered that to me. <br /><br />If I were to make any literary allusions, I would consider this book to have incorporated the story traditions of the tales of medieval knights, with a modern and often horrific spin. If I could describe Kate in any quick way, I would call her a knight-mercenary. She has the requisite sword, although she lacks the steed that usually goes with the package(To my pleasant surprise, there is quite a bit of horse-riding in this book, but Kate doesn't have her own horse). Unfortunately, we didn't get to see her wearing her armor. Maybe in the next books. Slasher, her blood-thirsty and sentient sword, reminded me of Stormbringer, the vampiric sword owned by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30036.Elric_of_Melnibon___The_Elric_Saga___1_" title="Elric of Melniboné (The Elric Saga, #1) by Michael Moorcock" rel="nofollow noopener">Elric of Melniboné</a>, written by Michael Moorcock, whom I became acquainted with earlier this fall.<br /><br />Any urban fantasy heroine has to have a potential spark, if you will. That's where Curran, The Beast Lord, comes in. He's impressive, let's leave it at that. He's not just a potential love interest, but a powerful ally. These two butt heads in the most delightful ways. As the Beast Lord, and a lion shapeshifter, Curran's used to being in charge, and Kate lives by the 'you're not the boss of me' philosophy. I look forward to more fighting alongside, and flirting with Curran in the next books.<br /><br /><br />This book is quite dark. Blood (and blood magic) and guts aplenty, dark deeds, dark magic, dark creatures. This is a book for a reasonably mature reader, in that regard. Being a big fan of Magic Noir (thank you, Brad, for letting me steal your fantastic term), I enjoyed those aspects. But I did wince at a few particularly gruesome scenes. The villain is a very disturbing individual, in more ways than one. Everything in this story has an edge to it. That's not a bad thing to this reader, since she enjoys a little darkness in her fiction. But if you tend to enjoy the lighter urban fantasy stories, you'd want to be prepared when you read this one. Now there is humor, but it's of the drier, more wry, and grimmer variety. If you like the hero to get banged up and injured quite a bit, you'll enjoy that about this novel. Kate definitely faces jeopardy, again and again. The stakes are particularly high in this novel, in ways that you need to read to find out.<br /><br />So, after so much rambling, I have to say that this urban fantasy fan has found a new series of which she intends to fully avail herself. Kate Daniels is my newest knight in shining armor. Let the adventures continue.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17649825650272456168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_61287560" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61287560" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61287560?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61287560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10174675195850384999"><b>This was a <i>really</i> dry book. I mean...<i>wow</i>!</b><br/>So, I originally read this (at the prompting of my BFF) back in 2010, and was so underwhelmed it took me 4 years to pick up the second book. And, <i>no</i> I didn't bother doing a re-read of book 1 beforehand. I was simply so <i>sick and tired</i> of all my friends telling me what a great series I was missing out on, that I just snatched up 2 and dove in.<br/><b>I fully expected to hate it.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488288005ra/22097769.gif' width='350' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>However, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1811543.Magic_Burns__Kate_Daniels___2_' title='Magic Burns (Kate Daniels, #2) by Ilona Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magic Burns</a> was fantastic, and set me on the path of becoming a rabid fan of n</span>
  <span id="freeText10174675195850384999" style="display:none"><b>This was a <i>really</i> dry book. I mean...<i>wow</i>!</b><br>So, I originally read this (at the prompting of my BFF) back in 2010, and was so underwhelmed it took me 4 years to pick up the second book. And, <i>no</i> I didn't bother doing a re-read of book 1 beforehand. I was simply so <i>sick and tired</i> of all my friends telling me what a great series I was missing out on, that I just snatched up 2 and dove in.<br><b>I fully expected to hate it.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488288005ra/22097769.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>However, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1811543.Magic_Burns__Kate_Daniels___2_" title="Magic Burns (Kate Daniels, #2) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns</a> was fantastic, and set me on the path of becoming a rabid fan of not only <i>this</i> series, but of <i>anything</i> the Ilona Andrews duo writes. And even though I've pretty much read everything else that I can get my hands on, I'd <i>still</i> never attempted a re-read of <b>Magic Bites</b>. All I could remember was what a chore it felt like to slog through, and some vague <b>Here, Kitty, Kitty, Kitty...</b> reference to Kate and Curran's first meeting.<br><i>It was love at first sight for those two...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488288637ra/22097895.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So. Fast forward 7 years, and here I am. <b>
  <i>Finally</i>
</b> going back to see what happened to kick off one of my favorite series ever! I felt sure it would be awesome! And in my mind, I looked a bit like <b>THIS</b> while jumping into the story:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488289328ra/22097993.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The reality was a bit more...<b>THIS:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488289328ra/22097994.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Ok. So, <i>yes</i>, it was better this time around. Now that I know what the world is like, see where all of this is going with Kate and Curran, know what's up with all of the cryptic references to her father and her blood, and recognize characters that will become important staples in this universe in later books - it wasn't chore to get through it.<br><b>However.</b><br>I still say this is one of the worst intro books ever. At least, to such a <i>fabulous</i> series.<br>The first book of a new series should WOW you. It should be so <i>delicious</i> that it slaps you across the face, knocks you off your feet, makes you want to come back for more. <br><i>This?</i> <br><b>This was dry and crunchy with an oddly unspecific taste to it.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488292518ra/22098683.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This time around, I'd give it 4 stars because I love these characters SO much, and seeing them meet and fight was unbelievably worthwhile. But there's still a <i>teeny-tiny</i> part of my brain that realizes this book was boring enough that it took me 7 years to bring myself to do a re-read.<br>I wish I could just be like, <b>
  <i>Nah, this was great! I don't know what you fools are talking about!</i>
</b> And admitting that I understand why a lot of people don't continue with the series after reading this <i>pains me</i>...truly.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488292173ra/22098632.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, so here's the deal: if you read this and thought it sucked, for the love of God, just read the second book before you decide to give up. And, NO, don't go back and try to do a re-read of this one first! Go...just <i>go</i>! Move on to book 2, and the recaps will get you through.<br>For anyone who truly <i>did</i> enjoy this book the first time around, know that I'm <i>not</i> saying it's crap, just that I don't believe it does a good job showing how awesome these characters or this world will become in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10174675195850384999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1423338372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423338372" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1423338372?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Katerina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/28376061-vippi">Vippi</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1423338372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17158450566307178043"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“These were unsafe times. But then in safer times, I'd be a woman without a job. The safe-tech world had little use for a magic-touting mercenary like me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Welcome to a world where <b>magic and technology fight</b> to gain the upper hand. Where <b>necromancers control vampires</b> and <b>every nightmarish mythical creature turns out to be real</b>, eager to devour human flesh.<br/>Welcome to Atlanta.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405867922ra/10462902.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>The story</u>
</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My name is Kate Daniels. Greg Feldman was my legal guardian and the closest thing to a fam</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17158450566307178043" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“These were unsafe times. But then in safer times, I'd be a woman without a job. The safe-tech world had little use for a magic-touting mercenary like me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Welcome to a world where <b>magic and technology fight</b> to gain the upper hand. Where <b>necromancers control vampires</b> and <b>every nightmarish mythical creature turns out to be real</b>, eager to devour human flesh.<br>Welcome to Atlanta.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405867922ra/10462902.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The story</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My name is Kate Daniels. Greg Feldman was my legal guardian and the closest thing to a family I've had for many years. I want to find the scum who killed him.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Kate Daniels is a mercenary, hired to take care of supernatural problems. When her guardian is brutally murdered but no one seems to know by whom and why, she takes matters in her own hands and crosses paths with shapechanger lords, necromancers and vampires trying to get answers. But when she is targeted by a creature more devious and ruthless than anything she's ever encoutered, she has to make choices that will affect others and decide who is worthy of her trust and who deserves to be run through by her magic blade.<br><br><b>
  <u>Thoughts</u>
</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38619.Magic_Bites__Kate_Daniels___1_" title="Magic Bites (Kate Daniels, #1) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bites</a> was the introduction to an <b>action-packed</b>, <b>drama-free</b> and <b>gruesome</b> saga. I must admit there were many times I felt <b>confused</b> and my brain hurt from the effort to understand, because the world-building was slow with many questions unanswered, and that's the reason I rated it with 4 stars. That being said, <b>I immensely enjoyed this book</b>! Despite being difficult to get into, it kept me hooked and I was eager to learn more, to dive into magic adventures and bloody fights! I've read my fair share of urban fantasy but this series was different from my regular YA ones. More <b>mature, darker, crueller and slightly disgusting</b> (unless you are unfazed by mutilated corpses and a huge variety of body fluids), yet <b>fascinating</b> and <b>extremely engaging</b>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440724490ra/16016237.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The characters</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What kind of a woman greets the Beast Lord with 'here, kitty, kitty'?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>That's Kate. Sarcastic, confident and smart-ass, she'll face danger without blinking and she'll slay anything that gets in her way. She's not a team player and she can't tolerate any form of authority. She doesn't have any friends, her life evolves around blood and magic. And she has a sword named Slayer. That's what we call <b>badass</b>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447105161ra/16955944.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But Kate isn't the only badass here. How about a shapechanger whose beast form is a lion, sexy as hell, arrogant and stubborn <b>alpha-male asshole</b>? Meet Curran, also known as <b>sex-on-a-stick</b>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422213243ra/13472542.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>While romance isn't the main focus of Magic Bites, you can sense that things will get intimate between Kate and Curran because <b>holy.hawt.chemistry.Batman!</b> They barely tolerate each other because they're so much alike, and they constantly bicker and that's why when they finally get together I expect explosions and fireworks!<br><br>If you're in the mood for a <b>darker urban fantasy book full of blood and gore</b>, then don't hesitate to grab the Kate Daniels series!<br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/katerina_papas/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/KaterinaPapas" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="http://booknest.eu/index.php/component/k2/item/96-magicbites" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17158450566307178043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1093425969" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1093425969" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1093425969?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5623788-missevi-can-t-commit-to-a-book">missEvi [can&#39;t commit to a book]</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1093425969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1478999741843819611"><strong>Curran, where have you been all my life?</strong><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414730604i/11683573.jpg' width='500' height='490' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Because he simply stole my heart from the very beginning. <em>And I’m usually not even into shapeshifters!</em><br/><br/>Must be due to his sense of humour, handsomeness and, of course, alpha personality and status.<br/><blockquote>
  <strong>His Majesty Curran,</strong>
  <br/>
  <strong> The chosen Lord of Free Beasts,</strong>
  <br/>
  <strong> Requests your presence at the meeting of his Pack</strong>
  <br/>
  <strong> At 22:00 of this night.</strong>
</blockquote><br/>Damn you, lucky Kate. I wish I could pay him a visit myself.<br/><blockquote>
  <strong>“Oh, it's you," Curran's voice said quietly. "I thoug</strong></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1478999741843819611" style="display:none"><strong>Curran, where have you been all my life?</strong><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414730604i/11683573.jpg" width="500" height="490" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Because he simply stole my heart from the very beginning. <em>And I’m usually not even into shapeshifters!</em><br><br>Must be due to his sense of humour, handsomeness and, of course, alpha personality and status.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>His Majesty Curran,</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> The chosen Lord of Free Beasts,</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> Requests your presence at the meeting of his Pack</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> At 22:00 of this night.</strong>
</blockquote><br>Damn you, lucky Kate. I wish I could pay him a visit myself.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>“Oh, it's you," Curran's voice said quietly. "I thought it was an elephant.”</strong>
</blockquote><br>Curran has a really interesting personality. And not a single moment of boredom, throughout the read, was present, especially when he was around.<br><br>Kate Daniels may remind you of some other strong, kick-ass, sarcastic and brutal honest heroines in other UF series. EXCEPT, this girl is not TSTL or too focused on her work to look for romantic love and, also, doesn’t jump on every guy she meets, like many other UF protagonists I have met.<br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>“Why a raven?"</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> "To honor my father."</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> "The writing under it, is that Cyrillic?"</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> "Yes."</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> "What does it say?"</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> "Dar Vorona. Gift of the Raven. I am my father's gift."</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> "The raven is holding a bloody sword."</strong>
  <br>
  <strong> "I never said it was a nice gift.”</strong>
</blockquote><br>What is interesting about this main character is that, for the first time in my life or so, I actually never predicted what she would say or answer. She was completely unpredictable, a little reckless sometimes I admit, but definitely entertaining and intelligent too.<br><br>The world-building is one of the things I liked best about this first book in a series, along with every element composing it, such as the characters, the different types of supernatural creatures, the magic which was fitting the plot well, the mystery which held me captive until the very last page, the pacing that was at a perfect speed and the little bit of romance that the author aloud us to witness.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>“You will tell me what you know now," he said.</strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>"Or?"</strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>He said nothing, so I elaborated. "See, this kind of threat usually has an 'or' attached to it. Or an 'and'. 'Tell me and I'll allow you to live' or something like that.”</strong>
</blockquote><br>I saw some reviewers complaining about the writing style which they mostly found not of their liking, but I truly thought it was good. I do admit that the author’s way of describing characters wasn’t impressive at all and could get pretty boring since it consisted a lot of doing an enumeration but, since it doesn’t happen that often, it didn’t come to actually bother me.<br><br>You know, truth be told, I regret a bit not starting this sooner, since I absolutely ended up LOVING IT. The atmosphere was likable, the protagonist perfectly right for this kind of story and everything inside it had a meaning and wasn’t there to just fill some empty space. So, I would highly highly recommend this story to you, if you normally enjoy urban fantasy books.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1478999741843819611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156913295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18192478826977375213">🐈 <b>The Adventures Of A Brave Little Kitty Buddy Rerererereread</b> (TAOABLKBR™) with the IA Addicts 🐈<br/><br/>➽ <b>
  <u>And the moral of this particular rererererereread is:</u>
</b> Kate Bloody Shrimping Daniels = <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557773017i/27500901.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Bloody shrimping QED and stuff</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>⚔ <b>
  <u>The Grand IAA™ KD Buddy Rerererereread Extravaganza</u>

  <u>And the moral of this particular rererereread is:</u>
</b> one tiny little KD fix and all is right in the world again. <b>Bye now</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[Original review]<br><br><i>☆☆☆ Post-Shift Productions proudly present ☆☆☆</i><br><b>Just Another Day in the Life of Kate Daniels</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422176678i/13467151.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>►<b>8.00 a.m.:</b> <b>Chilling at home</b>. Looks like there's something on your wall. Well hello there you <b>friendly neighbourhood spiderman</b>. Throw a knife, slice a throat. <b>Today's going to be a good day</b>.<br>► <b>8.30 a.m.:</b> Greg. Dead. <b>Shit</b>.<br>► <b>9.00 a.m.:</b> Pay the <b>Knights of Merciful Aid</b> a visit. Meet Scumbag Ted of The Debatable Fashion Sense. Discuss your <b>investigative techniques</b>: <i>annoy the people involved until the guilty party tries to make you go away.</i> <b>Always works wonders</b>.<br>► <b>9.30 a.m.:</b> Meet a hot guy with a toothpaste name. Try to <b>radiate integrity and decency of character</b>. Doesn't work. Give him your knockout smile. Misfires. <b>Damn</b>.<br>► <b>10.00 a.m.:</b> Talk to <b>Anna</b>. She just had a vision of you sitting cross-legged on the grass, eating a corpse. <b>Nice</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430250488i/14698083.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>10.30 a.m.:</b> Oh look! A big cat! <b>Here kitty kitty kitty!</b> Give the beast your best <b>cryptic smile</b>. Try to impress him with Slayer's useless but very cool white glow. <b>Fail miserably</b>.<br>► <b>11.00 a.m.:</b> Pay <b>Saiman</b> a visit. Watch him go from bombshell blonde to <b>barbarian king</b> in less time than it takes to blink. <b>Throw up in your mouth a little</b>.<br>► <b>11.30 a.m.:</b> Finally manage to get some rest. Head to shower. <b>The phone rings</b>. Step out of shower. It's Mr Hot Toothpaste asking you out. Wow, did you just say yes to a date? Yes you did. Head back to shower. <b>The phone rings. Damn</b>. Step out of shower. It's Maxine letting you know Scumbag Ted of The Debatable Fashion Sense wants to see you ASAP. Oh goody. Head back to shower. <b>The phone rings. Somebody kill me now</b>. Step out of shower. It's Jim. Gives you hell but puts up with your shit. He doesn't have a choice. <b>Who else is going to help his furry ass anyway?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430250488i/14698084.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>12.00 a.m.:</b> Put on your <b>Thugs Are Us outfit</b>. Pay your new Pack friends a visit. Piss His Furry Majesty off a little. <b>He better get used to it</b>.<br>► <b>12.30 a.m.:</b> Get yourself a <b>teenage werewolf sidekick</b>. Go visit the People's shithole. Look at lovely <b>vampire family pictures</b>: intestines, brain, heart, bladder, colon, oesophagus, lungs, liver, kidneys. It's like a build-your-own-vampire Ikea kit! <b>Very cool</b>.<br>► <b>1.00 p.m.:</b> Cut a freakish, ancient <b>vampire's head off</b>. Take it home to try a new recipe. Add some herbs. A drop of blood. Chant a little. <b>Wakey wakey vampire head!</b><br>► <b>1.30 p.m.:</b> Surprise visit from <b>Mr Hot Toothpaste</b>. Chat about tattoos, ravens and the <b>odds of getting an orgasm with a blind date</b>. Hey, it looks like someone is trying to take advantage of an injured, naked woman. <b>About time!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416932225ra/12120157.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>2.00 p.m.:</b> Time to finally <b>get some rest</b>. Someone knocks on your door. <b>What now?</b> Oh look, the Beast Lord! And here you were thinking it would be <b>someone important</b>.<br>► <b>2.30 p.m.:</b> Field trip to <b>Unicorn Lane</b> with your furry friends. His Fussiness compares you to an elephant. <b>Try and refrain from kicking his ass</b>.<br>► <b>3.00 p.m.:</b> Meet a lovely <b>Mistress of the Dead</b>. Cut cut cut, slice slice slice, cleave cleave cleave. Play the disembowelment game. <b>Fun times</b>.<br>► <b>3.30 p.m.:</b> Oh look! A <b>blanket of undead</b> on the ceiling! <b>Rip a heart out</b>, mix a blood cocktail, pilot a few vamps, play with fire, pass out. <b>Same old, same old</b>.<br>► <b>4.00 p.m.:</b> Witness the <b>Beast Lord soaking in all his naked glory</b>. Want to jump in? Err, no thank you. <b>Places to go, things to do and all that</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429830969i/14635659.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>4.30 p.m.:</b> Get ready for a <b>date with Mr Hot Toothpaste</b>. Dress up. Fancy restaurant. <b>Boring, boring, BORED</b>. Well if that isn't His Furry Highness sitting across the room from you! <b>Here, have some milk kitty cat</b>.<br>► <b>5.00 p.m.:</b> Home at last. <b>Get some sleep</b>. Wake up feeling refreshed. Err, is that a human head on a stick? In your yard? <b>Will this day never end?</b><br>► <b>5.30 p.m.:</b> Oh look! A <b>giant bone puzzle!</b> It's just like sorting out dirty laundry! Vamps on the right, shifters on the left! <b>Good times</b>.<br>► <b>6.00 p.m.:</b> Wrongly accuse an innocent man. <b>Feel like shit</b>. Get drunk. Uh-oh, bad idea. Looks like <b>you're on the menu tonight</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430249964i/14697994.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>6.30 p.m.:</b> Make a <b>pact with the devil</b>. Piss His Furriness off. <b>So what else is new?</b><br>► <b>7.00 p.m.:</b> Time for a <b>costume party</b>. The Beast Lord wishes you good luck. I. What. You. Huh? <b>Concentrate Kate, concentrate</b>.<br>► <b>7.30 p.m.:</b> Rotting flesh, <b>putrid juices</b>, swarms of flies, half-animals on a telepathic leash. <b>Why me?</b><br>► <b>8.00 p.m.:</b> Cut cut cut, slice slice slice. Make a little magic, speak a few power words, play with fire again. <b>Oh look! A see-through villain!</b> Take that you vicious bastard! <b>Feel like you're dying a little</b>.<br>► <b>8.30 p.m.:</b> Regain consciousness. <b>Unexpected hellish nursemaid</b>. No nails. New job. The Beast Lord can't hammer shit. <b>Oh boy</b>.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422119861i/13458929.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>• <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1136556683" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 3</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222658742" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Strikes</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 4</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222662503" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bleeds</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 5</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156907200" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Slays</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 6</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087380222" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Rises</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 7</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222671908" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Breaks</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 8</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088122695" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Shifts</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 9</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1388386563" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Binds</a> ★★★★★<br>• <b>Book 10</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767301739" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Triumphs</a> ★★★★</span>

<div id="review_83347289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83347289" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83347289?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">urban fantasy lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Heather, Penny
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83347289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11723285291317243287">Another second chance reread. Another DNF. I can’t believe I put some much work into ranting about this book. All I can say today is that it bores me. <br/><br/><b>Original review</b><br/><br/>I've read enough urban fantasy to know that the genre is extremely formulaic, just like, let's say, the genre of historical romance. Basically, you are aware of what exactly you are going to get from the get-go. The difficulty here is to find a series whose standard mix of ass-kicking heroine/amusing cast of secondary characters/lor</span>
  <span id="freeText11723285291317243287" style="display:none">Another second chance reread. Another DNF. I can’t believe I put some much work into ranting about this book. All I can say today is that it bores me. <br /><br /><b>Original review</b><br /><br />I've read enough urban fantasy to know that the genre is extremely formulaic, just like, let's say, the genre of historical romance. Basically, you are aware of what exactly you are going to get from the get-go. The difficulty here is to find a series whose standard mix of ass-kicking heroine/amusing cast of secondary characters/lore/mystery/paranormal hunk that suits your personal preferences. Unfortunately, I will have to put "Magic Bites" into the pile of urban fantasy I doubt I will ever get back to, along with Richelle Mead's "Storm Born" and Patricia Briggs' "Moon Called."<br /><br />The weakest part of the book is definitely the writing. I can see how Ilona Andrews might have lost numerous readers within just the first couple of chapters. She throws us in the middle of her world without explaining anything at all. Only pages later do we get enough information to understand previous events. A perfect example is the opening scene of "Magic Bites" where Kate throws a knife into a vampire's throat and then this vampire starts talking to her in a voice of some other character. Finally two chapters later you find out that in Andrews' world vampires are basically brainless zombies who are operated by necronavigators. This kind of thing happens repeatedly. Some readers might enjoy such cryptic type of writing based on extensive withholding of information. I personally don't find it enjoyable, unless it's written by Margaret Atwood or Megan Whalen Turner. However in this case I don't think the effect is intentional, it seems to be more indicative of poor writing skills. I might have overlooked the bad writing (after all, you do eventually get a better understanding of the world and start keeping up with the events), if only I felt attached to the world or the characters. No luck here unfortunately.<br /><br />Patricia Briggs calls "Magic Bites" <i>"an edgy, dark fantasy, touched with just the right amount of humor"</i> in her blurb on the book cover. The novel is not particularly (or at all) humorous, but it is dark indeed. In fact, "Magic Bites" is probably the darkest and goriest urban fantasy I've come across so far. Andrews doesn't shy away from incorporating split open chests, exposed colons, dead flesh eating monsters, etc. in her novel. So if you are not into this kind of thing, you might want to reconsider reading this book.<br /><br />I appreciate the author's attempt to reshape traditional werewolf/vampire lore with a touch of Slavic mythology added in. Sometimes it works (I liked the shapechanger concept), sometimes it seems ridiculous ("feeding" your sword a mixture of wheat with some iron bits). I personally find this world ugly and very vaguely defined. For instance, I still have no understanding of what exactly "magic" is. Is it some kind of energy force? Who can be in possession of magic? How is it used? I've seen it operate cars, I've seen it applied telepathically, through incantation, via a sword, with the help of herbs in this book. I still have no idea what it is. I would also love to gain a better understanding of the relationship between the human and magic world. Do they co-exist? How much are they aware of each other? What is humans' attitude towards the magical creatures and vice versa? Or I would love to know what exactly the Guild and its diviners and protectors do. Or what Kate does as a mercenary. <br /><br />And finally, the main character. Kate Daniels will appeal to you if you like your heroines tough, very gloomy, with no sense of humor and irresistibly appealing to all the males in the vicinity (to be fair, this is a common theme in urban fantasy). I would have liked her more if Andrews didn't write her so ever defiant and in constant need to get confrontational with every person (man) of power around her. She softens up a little bit towards the end of the book, but unfortunately too late in the game for me to change my opinion about her.<br /><br />Overall, "Magic Bites" didn't quite work for me. The mystery kept me turning pages, but I finished the book without a desire to continue on with the series. It doesn't mean, however, that this novel will not work for you. It might, especially if you like your urban fantasy dark and gory and your sword-wielding heroines tough and defiant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11723285291317243287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=vampires-and-werewolves-oh-my">vampires-and-werewolves-oh-my</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=you-go-girl-kickass-heroine">you-go-girl-kickass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=sometimes-fun-beats-profound">sometimes-fun-beats-profound</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer997706823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12302166896672281241"><b>99c Kindle sale, March 10, 2020.</b> The first book in the Kate Daniels series! It's pretty good urban fantasy, but the series definitely improves and builds on itself as it goes along, so keep your expectations tempered for the first couple of books, and don't give up, at least until you've read the third book. <br/><br/>3.5 stars, rounding up. In an alternative version of our world, technology and magic are at odds: when a "magic fluctuation" hits, most technological items (cell phones, cars, anything elect</span>
  <span id="freeText12302166896672281241" style="display:none"><b>99c Kindle sale, March 10, 2020.</b> The first book in the Kate Daniels series! It's pretty good urban fantasy, but the series definitely improves and builds on itself as it goes along, so keep your expectations tempered for the first couple of books, and don't give up, at least until you've read the third book. <br><br>3.5 stars, rounding up. In an alternative version of our world, technology and magic are at odds: when a "magic fluctuation" hits, most technological items (cell phones, cars, anything electrical) stop working, but sooner or later the magic wave ends and technology kicks in again. Smart people finds ways to get along whether magic or technology happens to be ascendant, like Kate Daniels, who carries a sword - fondly named Slayer - and is capable of kicking pretty much anyone's ass at any given time. Someone has killed Kate's friend and one-time mentor, Greg Feldman, and Kate is determined to find out who it is. But her investigation becomes increasingly dangerous to herself and those who are helping her.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407165216i/10649283.jpg" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>Magic Bites</i> is basically a detective story set in an urban fantasy world, complete with vampires and werewolves, but they're vampires and werewolves (or, more accurately, shapechangers, since many of them are not wolves but rats, leopards, lions, etc.) like I've never seen or read about before. I'm rounding up to four stars because the world-building with the fantasy part of the story is done so well here. It struck me as detailed, highly original, and very well integrated into the overall story. Vampires, for example, are near-mindless automatons controlled by humans who are trained to do so:<blockquote>. . . the mind of a vampire died the moment vampirism took hold. The vampires knew no pity and no fear; they couldn't be trained; they had no ego. On a developmental level they stood close to insects . . . An insatiable hunger for blood ruled them and they slaughtered everything in their path in their urge to quench it.</blockquote>Also this:<blockquote>The thing followed me on all fours. It was a vampire, but one so ancient that no trace of it having walked upright remained. . . Its face no longer bore any resemblance to a human. . . Rows of fangs gleamed against the blackness.</blockquote>Eeeek! Also eeeew!<br><br>There's a lot of snarky humor in this book, again kind of like a gumshoe detective story. When Kate is summoned to a meeting with the shapechangers she considers her options for self-protection:<blockquote>I paused, considered the arsenal available to me, put on thin wristbands loaded with silver needles, and took nothing else except Slayer. To get clear of two hundred enraged shapechangers I'd need a case of grenades and air support. There was no reason to weigh myself down with extra weapons. Then again, maybe I should take a knife. One knife, as a backup. Okay, two. And that's it. Armed and dressed to kill--or rather to die quickly but in style--I went . . .</blockquote>Overall, it's not terribly deep or insightful, but it's a fun read and I think it achieves very well what it's trying to be. And the series seriously improves by the third book.<br><br>Content notes: There are a fair number of F-bombs and some blatant sexual innuendos. And gory scenes. Also, rape trigger warning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12302166896672281241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
