<div id="review_717991004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/717991004" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717991004?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=adorable-alphas">adorable-alphas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717991004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3132050714151406915"><b>Sale Alert:</b> This is one of my all time favorite UF series, currently on sale 08Mar20 at amazon <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Magic-Bites-Kate-Daniels-Book-ebook/dp/B000SEH16E?_bbid=14235088&tag=bookbubemail6-20' rel='nofollow noopener'>$0.99</a><br/><br/><b>Kate Daniels Buddy Read/Reread starts April 27 with the gang at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148835-ilona-andrews-addicts-iaa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ilona Andrews Addicts (IAA)</a></b><br/><br/><i>Let the fun and games begin</i>, Yes it is still only a 3.5 star read but I really enjoyed it all over again. There is a little plotting issue that is fuzzy but overall great start to one of my favorite UF series. <i>Only beaten just slightly by books 1-5 of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/48206.Karen_Marie_Moning' title='Karen Marie Moning' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karen Marie Moning</a>'s Fever Series</i>.<br/><br/><b>3.5 Stars Re-read 25Jun</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3132050714151406915" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert:</b> This is one of my all time favorite UF series, currently on sale 08Mar20 at amazon <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Magic-Bites-Kate-Daniels-Book-ebook/dp/B000SEH16E?_bbid=14235088&amp;tag=bookbubemail6-20" rel="nofollow noopener">$0.99</a><br /><br /><b>Kate Daniels Buddy Read/Reread starts April 27 with the gang at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148835-ilona-andrews-addicts-iaa" rel="nofollow noopener">Ilona Andrews Addicts (IAA)</a></b><br /><br /><i>Let the fun and games begin</i>, Yes it is still only a 3.5 star read but I really enjoyed it all over again. There is a little plotting issue that is fuzzy but overall great start to one of my favorite UF series. <i>Only beaten just slightly by books 1-5 of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/48206.Karen_Marie_Moning" title="Karen Marie Moning" rel="nofollow noopener">Karen Marie Moning</a>'s Fever Series</i>.<br /><br /><b>3.5 Stars Re-read 25Jun2014 before the release of Magic Breaks</b><br /><br />I forgot the entire plot to this book and it was like reading it all over again. Sure I remembered <b>ALL</b> the interactions between Kate and Curran and I remember meeting Derek for the first time. But I had totally forgotten who the bad guy was and why. I guess we all know what I really cared about. I even forgot there was a Zombie Dragon!!!<b> A freaking Zombie Dragon</b> and I had totally forgotten about it….bad Robin…Bad.<br /><br />This was my first Ilona Andrews (IA) book (<i>I’ve read 14 now, including the novellas</i>) and it is also my lowest rated IA book. It all just gets better from here. They have come a long way as a writing team and I enjoyed this book maybe even a little more the second time through.<br /><br />I love the early Kate and all the posturing she and Curran do to prove who is top dog or cat as the case may be. The humor is still there but it gets so much better in the later books. I enjoyed the beginning a little more because I understand the magic or this world and I could focus on other details this time around.<br /><br />The 7th book Magic Breaks will be out the end of July and it completes an entire plot arc so if you are looking for a fun PRN/UF series I highly suggest this one, cheesy Narnia-esk cover not-with-standing .<br /><br /><b> Initial Review 21Sept13</b> <br />I’m going to admit that I put off reading this based solely on the cover for a long time. I saw the lion and thought, shades of Narnia, no thanks, I’ll pass. But, I was assured that couldn’t be further from the truth and was talked into reading it. So thanks to all those who peer pressured me, you know who you are. <br /><br />Kate Daniels takes a different approach to solving mysteries and getting things done.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Annoy principals involved until the guilty party decides to kill you.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Now in most books that <b>is</b> how the story works but the characters never use it as an actual strategy. That was the first reason I liked this book. Warning: the world in this book is really different from any other UPF I’ve read and it takes a little getting used to. The author doesn’t ever succumb to the info drop and just trusts the reader to wait as the world is uncovered bit by bit. It takes time to do it this way but in the end I like the result a lot better.<br /><br />This is a world where magic and technology sort of shift like the tides. When one is in full swing the other doesn’t really work. People have learned to live in two worlds that are together and separate all at the same time. Although somewhat confusing while you are figuring out the world that is being presented by the author it is fascinating and was almost as much a draw for me as the story line.<br /><br />Kate Daniels is a girl shrouded in some mystery and I can see from this first book that she is going to kick some butt throughout the series. She is not a damsel in distress although she is vulnerable at times. Magic Bites has started to set up her character quite well and while we get a glimpse at who Kate Daniels is I do have a feeling we have only scratched the surface. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“So you admit to being a walking stereotype?”<br />“It’s safer that way,” I said honestly.</i>
</b><br /><br />There is plenty going on as Kate tries to figure out who killed her guardian. She has been alone for so long that it is difficult to play well with others. Even though she is defiant of authority and often does or says things she knows she shouldn’t, Kate remains very likable which not every heroine can pull off. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Diplomacy was never my strong suit and my patience had run dry. I crouched and called out, “Here, kitty, kitty, kitty.”<i></i></i>
</b><br /><br />Teaming up with the local were-pack has some hardships of its own especially for Kate who can’t just lay down and show her belly to the alpha of the pack no matter how hot he is. A battle of wills at hand and Kate might just be in over her head.<br /><br />Overall the story was entertaining, I enjoyed getting to know Kate, Curran definitely has some possibilities and the world captured my imagination. I will definitely be reading on in the series to see where the larger story arc goes.</span>

<div id="review_1121362505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1121362505" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1121362505?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters">werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=girls-i-want-to-hang-out-with">girls-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=buddy-read-with-iaa">buddy-read-with-iaa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121362505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1195047370632694536">I reread this one with the girls at the Ilona Andrews Addicts group. And, strangely, I was slightly disappointed. Why? Well, I know this world and Kate so well now that I expected a magical wonderland when I read it again. But, there were problems that I didn't remember.<br/><br/><u>Problem 1: Worldbuilding</u><br/><br/>There were info-dumps galore. Pages and pages of them. But, we are never actually given a reason why the world changed from what we know now to a magic-infested one. There was no cataclysmic event, war, or</span>
  <span id="freeText1195047370632694536" style="display:none">I reread this one with the girls at the Ilona Andrews Addicts group. And, strangely, I was slightly disappointed. Why? Well, I know this world and Kate so well now that I expected a magical wonderland when I read it again. But, there were problems that I didn't remember.<br /><br /><u>Problem 1: Worldbuilding</u><br /><br />There were info-dumps galore. Pages and pages of them. But, we are never actually given a reason why the world changed from what we know now to a magic-infested one. There was no cataclysmic event, war, or virus that changed things. It just was.<br /><br /><u>Problem 2: The Alpha Asshole</u><br /><br />I've known Curran for umpteen books now and think of him as Mr. Awesome. But, I had totally forgotten that he started out as an insufferable asshole in this first book. I truly hated him and now I wish that Kate and him never get together. She deserves better. Like Hugh, for example. lol!<br /><br /><u>Problem 3: Overly Descriptive Scenes</u><br /><br />You know how I feel when an author takes a full page to describe the sunset: Stabby. That's right. I read because I use this thing called my imagination, therefore I can imagine the sunset on my own. Also, I don't care what exact shade the wood is or what flowers are in the vase in a room that is simply a place that they will stand in and talk for a few minutes. It doesn't matter. It doesn't help build the scene. Get to the point, dammit!<br /><br /><u>Conclusion</u><br /><br />All this is to say: maybe you can't go home again. It's never the way you remembered it.<br /><br />Do I still love Kate Daniels and everything else written by Ilona Andrews? Yes. And, hey, I admit that I'm a critical bitch. That's my best quality. I am just saying that I now realize that the series started off a little rocky. It is still an amazing series and Kate is still my favorite girl. And, I still want everyone to read this series. Just, maybe give it a couple of books, and then the magic will happen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1195047370632694536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_715402388" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715402388" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/715402388?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Evgeny by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715402388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2767267558943584936">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5600230-armina' rel='nofollow noopener'>Armina</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17237503-eilonwy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eilonwy</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Asya</a>. <br/><br/>By the time this book was published, Jim Butcher's Dresden Files series was already well-known with quite a lot of writers trying to copy it with the various degree of success. I am willing to bet any money Kate Daniels was inspired by Dresden Files, directly or indirectly. For this reason I will compare these two.<br/><br/>Here we have a female protagonist Kate Daniels who happened to be a mercenary who makes her living cleaning up magical problems. You see, she</span>
  <span id="freeText2767267558943584936" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5600230-armina" rel="nofollow noopener">Armina</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17237503-eilonwy" rel="nofollow noopener">Eilonwy</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya" rel="nofollow noopener">Asya</a>. <br /><br />By the time this book was published, Jim Butcher's Dresden Files series was already well-known with quite a lot of writers trying to copy it with the various degree of success. I am willing to bet any money Kate Daniels was inspired by Dresden Files, directly or indirectly. For this reason I will compare these two.<br /><br />Here we have a female protagonist Kate Daniels who happened to be a mercenary who makes her living cleaning up magical problems. You see, she lives in a post-apocalyptic Atlanta with her world switching back and forth between technological based (our own) and magic based with a lot of nasty magical creatures and bad wizards creating all kinds of trouble. For me this set up was much more believable than Dresden's where people live side-by-side with magic and just choose to ignore it exists. Kate's mentor and friend was killed, and she is hell-bent on finding the culprit.<br /><br />I will be the first one to admit it is much easier to write a male protagonist who solves magic problems by exterminating them than a female one. In the former case one can combine Conan the Barbarian with Rambo and get somewhat believable - if completely one-dimensional - character. In the latter case the same guy can be slapped with a name Peggy or Mary (the examples do exist), but all the remaining shreds of believability would go out of the window. I am happy to say Kat Daniels as a female kick-ass protagonist works - almost. She does have her weaknesses and she admits to having them.<br /><br />There are a lot of drop-dead gorgeous women and extremely handsome guys in the book with quite a few of the latter falling head over heels for Kate, but these are required tropes for the genre. Speaking about falling in love, there is some romance in there, but not enough to qualify for paranormal romance status. I am really glad to say the romance never got in the way of the plot.<br /><br />There is something else which was refreshing about the series. The major part of urban fantasy monsters come from Celtic mythology which became kind of old at this time. Kate meets monsters bases on Slavic (this obviously comes from one of the authors being Russian), Chinese, and some other myths from around the world.<br /><br />Kate's wisecracking is on the level with that of Harry Dresden; she does not take herself seriously even in the face of a great danger ("Here kitty, do you want some milk?").<br /><br />As a debut book it is stronger then Dresden Files. It is also a very easy and fast read. Regarding the negative points - other than the ones I already mentioned - the main villain seems to come out of nowhere and was not believable at all. My rating would be slightly above 3.5 stars, but I always cut some slack for the first published book, so 4 stars it is. <br /><br />This review is a copy/paste of my BookLikes one: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gene.booklikes.com/post/960649/while-most-of-the-genre-s-cliches-are-here-the-book-does-not-suck">http://gene.booklikes.com/post/960649...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2767267558943584936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</b><br/><br/>Kate is brilliant! A little cocky at the beginning of the book but she gets over it a</span>
  <span id="freeText17056229440167458473" style="display:none">Okay, okay... I admit the book was good and I was terribly wrong for not reading it sooner! All my fears were misplaced!!<br><br><b>Possible Spoilers coming up</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“He finished the bandage and was examining it critically.<br>"You know those things are unreliable." His voice held just a touch of reproach.<br>“Eleven out of twelve work fine. I’d say that’s better chances than getting an orgasm with a blind date and women still try.” </i>
</b><br><br>Kate is brilliant! A little cocky at the beginning of the book but she gets over it after the first two hundred disasters. She is tough, smart, mouthy and a little arrogant. She is my favorite kind of heroine. She doesn't give in to lengthy emotional blabbering or emotional breakdowns so I love her!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455310306i/18086683.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“The monster licked his lips, long lines of whiskers twitching, and spoke in a deep growl. "Pretty, aren't I?" Curran. In midform. I broke from his gaze. "Adorable.”</i>
</b><br><br>I love Curran. I can write all the reasons but in the end it comes down to gorgeous, arrogant, no emotional baggage, no scarred hero just male awesomeness.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379795939i/611778._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked the supportive characters all except Crest. I found that guy oily! My favorites were Derek and Nick.<br><br>The story was good after you got the world Andrews has created in order.It was fast paced, well written and with enough twists to keep you guessing. I look forward to the next ones and knowing what exactly Kate is!*happy dance*(love the gif)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411634ra/808886.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>************02/03/2014 UPDATE************</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don't get why Curran was inclined to believe Kate only if Crest was the bad guy. Stubborn idiot. And why it was her fault that he wasn't. She wasn't the one who said that Crest was the one. <span id="freeTextContainer13340692537582523977"><b>...and then you read a book by a pro, and you're all: fuuuuuuuuuck.</b><br/><br/>s'not perfect.<br/><br/>acute symptoms of firstbookinaseriesitis.<br/><br/>but lemme just fanboi about the writing for a minute, ok?<br/><br/>propulsive plotting: one thing leads naturally to another. the solution to one problem creates another. the solution to that creates yet another.<br/><br/>the false-denoument was a nice touch, but a little too early—a quick glance at my reading progress made it easy to dismiss the neatly 'solved' mystery immediately.<br/><br/>but <i>man.</i><br/><br/>you s</span>
  <span id="freeText13340692537582523977" style="display:none"><b>...and then you read a book by a pro, and you're all: fuuuuuuuuuck.</b><br /><br />s'not perfect.<br /><br />acute symptoms of firstbookinaseriesitis.<br /><br />but lemme just fanboi about the writing for a minute, ok?<br /><br />propulsive plotting: one thing leads naturally to another. the solution to one problem creates another. the solution to that creates yet another.<br /><br />the false-denoument was a nice touch, but a little too early—a quick glance at my reading progress made it easy to dismiss the neatly 'solved' mystery immediately.<br /><br />but <i>man.</i><br /><br />you spend all your time reading amateur stuff and struggling with your own amateur stuff—and then you read a thing, and you see who published it, and how many reviews it has, and what the ratings average is, and how many books came after it...<br /><br />and you just know.<br /><br />you can tell right away. first page.<br /><br />it was written by a pro.<br /><br />recommended.</span>

    <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party"><img alt="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562621595p2/10923016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Karlyflower *The Vampire Ninja, Luminescent Monster &amp; Wendigo Nerd Goddess of Canada (according to The Hulk)* by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=bewitch-you-soon">bewitch-you-soon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=dig-your-teeth-in">dig-your-teeth-in</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17243568-karlyflower-the-vampire-ninja-luminescent-monster-wendigo-nerd-godde?shelf=little-fae-today">little-fae-today</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1447635719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer544688971446836247"><b>3 <i>Here-kitty-kitty</i> Stars</b> <br/><br/>There is an inherent issue with having an Urban Fantasy novel that is only 260 pages long, in my opinion. And that issue is that there is <b>far</b> too much world information that has be introduced to the reader to avoid falling into the dreaded Info Dump territory; <u>Magic Bites</u> stumbles into that territory a little too much for my liking. I don’t know that I have ever said I wished that an UF novel was longer, but in this case I do because with the added length it may have bee</span>
  <span id="freeText544688971446836247" style="display:none"><b>3 <i>Here-kitty-kitty</i> Stars</b> <br><br>There is an inherent issue with having an Urban Fantasy novel that is only 260 pages long, in my opinion. And that issue is that there is <b>far</b> too much world information that has be introduced to the reader to avoid falling into the dreaded Info Dump territory; <u>Magic Bites</u> stumbles into that territory a little too much for my liking. I don’t know that I have ever said I wished that an UF novel was longer, but in this case I do because with the added length it may have been easier to <i>show</i> me (rather than tell me) the differences between Kate’s world and my own world. <br><br>The writing in this novel is rather simplistic, however, it flows well and has a natural progression from situation to situation that I have to admire. A LOT. I never felt like this story was awkward or forced, in any way. Sometimes I’ve felt like an author foisted a situation onto their character that was fake feeling or served a dramatic agenda; there was none of that here. I can’t say how much I appreciate having a convoluted story that feels like a natural web of moments weaving themselves into a conclusion of a mystery, it is a very lovely talent to possess. <br><br><b>Kate Daniels, You are a badass of the first Order! </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468523571ra/19718088.gif" width="450" height="191" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>(You should take it as a supreme compliment when I use a River Tam gif to express your badassary!)<br><br>I look forward to continuing with this series. I quite enjoyed Kate’s snarky attitude and her banter with Curran is exquisite. I can’t wait to find out about the hinted-to secret that makes Kate carry around gasoline on her person at all times. <br><br><i>He gave me a puzzled look. “I’m the one protecting you. You be careful.”<br>I shook my head. I finally got my knight in shining armour. Too bad he was a teenage werewolf. </i><br><b>*snorts*</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468523571ra/19718089.gif" width="500" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Thanks to my lovely ghouls for agreeing to buddy-read this with me and I would apologize for finishing it way ahead of everyone, AGAIN, but we are not supposed to apologize for such things anymore. ♥ <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470752378i/19961068._SY540_.jpg" width="350.4" height="467.4" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>------PRE-REVIEW------<br>This wonderful friend of mine gave me a second-hand copy of this for Christmas.... so there is a buddy-read in my future ;)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454519835ra/17975991.gif" width="245" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Buddy-read with some of my favourites - My Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows, BC, Future-Gurl and Trish - set to commence July 11th! Let the cherry popping begin!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="544688971446836247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2592537659" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2592537659" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2592537659?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=pnr-uf">pnr-uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2592537659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17367172303702840280"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>Remember when the <i>Anita Blake </i>series was good, back when she wasn't the Special Snowflake Queen of Sex'n'Superpowers™? (Seriously, have you read the new books? How is her vagina not permanently on fire from all that friction? Also, girl has more special moves than freaking Ditto.) Remember how the series was edgy and erotic and did not condescend to its female audience? Remember how Anita used to kick ass? Remember when there were just T</span>
  <span id="freeText17367172303702840280" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>Remember when the <i>Anita Blake </i>series was good, back when she wasn't the Special Snowflake Queen of Sex'n'Superpowers™? (Seriously, have you read the new books? How is her vagina not permanently on fire from all that friction? Also, girl has more special moves than freaking Ditto.) Remember how the series was edgy and erotic and did not condescend to its female audience? Remember how Anita used to kick ass? Remember when there were just TWO love interests and not an entire Siouxie and the Banshees concert-worth of Gothic rejects in frilly shirts suffering from existential crises? Ilona Andrews remembers. Enter Kate Daniels.<br><br>
  <br>
<br>Ilona Andrews has a huuuuuuge cult following. I got indoctrinated almost two years ago with the <i>Hidden Legacy </i>series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1994148277" rel="nofollow noopener">BURN FOR ME</a> was the book that got me back into urban fantasy). After speeding through the rest of the series like a cocaine addict burning through their stash, crying ecstatically over the series' rumored (and now <i>confirmed </i>continuation), and frantically working my way through the rest of the Esteemed Ilona Andrews Hoard
  ™, I finally found my way to reading the much-hyped and very intimidating <i>Kate Daniels </i>series. This series has freaking <i>fans</i> with a capital F.
<br><br>
  
    <br>
  
<br>
  It's a little scary, because I was looking at the publication date and this book came out when I was still in high school. Despite being over ten years old, though, the book still feels fresh. Part of that is because it hasn't become dated like a lot of other older PNRs. This is because in Kate Daniel's world, magic and technology are in conflict (they short each other out), and currently magic is at its zenith, so technology has yielded to swords, horses, leylines, and magical abilities. Holy father, Batman.
<br><br>
  
    <br>
  
<br>
  Kate has decided to seek revenge for the murder of her Guardian, using her own magical powers and her trusty sword as tools. But revenge isn't simple. The murderer has covered their tracks well, and worse yet - they also appear to be responsible for the serial killings of several shape-shifters, humans, and vampires in the area. What seemed like a simple goal befitting the most basic of heroes' journey plots suddenly becomes a supernatural Gordian knot riddled with sexy shape-shifters and necromancers (oh my). Andrews doesn't hold back on the gore, either. This book packs a mean body count, and you, the reader, are sitting right in the Splash Zone. (And that ain't water.)
<br><br>
  
    <br>
  
<br>
  So, my Completely Unbiased and Possibly Unwelcome Opinion

  
    ™ on this book is... that it was good but not great. People were telling me that this series is <i>much better than Hidden Legacy (OMFG)</i>
  

  
    
      , and maybe that's true for the later books in the series, but honestly, BURN FOR ME has a much stronger hook. And as fun as Kate Daniels is, she doesn't have the emotional depth and aching humanity that made Nevada such a treat (and made her gradual transformation over the course of the three books that much more addictive and investing, as a result). She tosses off some good one-liners, but I don't really understand what makes her tick. She's a stiletto heel in human form: pretty, sharp, but not very empathetic or intriguing. Also, Curran is no Rogan (don't @ me). There, I said it.
    
  
<br><br>
  
    
      
        <br>
      
      <i>
        
      </i>
    
  
<br>
  
    
      Still, I'm curious to see where the books go from here.
    
  
<br><br>
  
    
      
        <br>
      
      <i>
        
      </i>
    
  
<br>
  
    
      
        <b>3.5 stars</b>
      
      <i>
        
      </i>
    
  
</span>
  <a data-text-id="17367172303702840280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1450656338" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11871571723137530276">Magic and technology. The world created in this book is so complex that it is hard to explain it or even just describe it. <br/><br/>There is one thing to remember: Magic beats Technology. It is always a winner.<br/><br/>I loved the book. It helped the fact that it is full of many hateful, but also many beloved monsters. And I know how to appreciate a good twisted monster LOL<br/><br/>Kate is a kickass heroine. She knows how to use her sword better than she knows how to walk in high heels. She is fierce, strong, reliable, fa</span>
  <span id="freeText11871571723137530276" style="display:none">Magic and technology. The world created in this book is so complex that it is hard to explain it or even just describe it. <br /><br />There is one thing to remember: Magic beats Technology. It is always a winner.<br /><br />I loved the book. It helped the fact that it is full of many hateful, but also many beloved monsters. And I know how to appreciate a good twisted monster LOL<br /><br />Kate is a kickass heroine. She knows how to use her sword better than she knows how to walk in high heels. She is fierce, strong, reliable, faithful to her friends – although she doesn’t have many friends. Basically she doesn’t trust humans or monsters easily. They have to fight for her trust. But when they are in, they are in for good.<br /><br />Curran is a beloved monster. He is a shapeshifter and a Beast Lord. Very controlling and very protective. He only wishes his pack wellbeing. <br /><br />In “Magic Bites” Curran and Kate will be introduced, they will fight a powerful Upir (a corpe-eater creature) and they will start their joined adventures. <br /><br />I guess the most famous quote from this book (maybe from the whole series) comes from Kate and must be:<br /><br />"Here kitty, kitty, kitty."</span>
  <a data-text-id="11871571723137530276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1391491308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391491308" />
    <a title="Gergana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana"><img alt="Gergana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439319393p2/5312798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1391491308?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gergana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gergana" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana">Gergana</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18427611-magic-bites">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1391491308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1719124775713444029">Early 2015<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245041.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It was just another day in the GoodReads community. I had just found out that you can add people as friends (yep, took me a few years...Buddy reading literally blew my mind!) and I was minding my own business, reading fantasy books as usual.<br/>When suddenly, a new message started popping out:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245042.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245043.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And that's how I found out about a series called <i>Kate Daniels</i>. Apparently, I was one of the very few who had no idea what the whole hype was all about. Before long, my updates page was buzzing with me</span>
  <span id="freeText1719124775713444029" style="display:none">Early 2015<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245041.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was just another day in the GoodReads community. I had just found out that you can add people as friends (yep, took me a few years...Buddy reading literally blew my mind!) and I was minding my own business, reading fantasy books as usual.<br>When suddenly, a new message started popping out:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245042.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245043.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And that's how I found out about a series called <i>Kate Daniels</i>. Apparently, I was one of the very few who had no idea what the whole hype was all about. Before long, my updates page was buzzing with messages, groups of people rereading the whole series and speculating on what will happen next! It reminded me of my experience with the Harry Potter books with one major problem - I wasn't part of the Fandom! I was missing out on something huge?! It's like the feeling you get when all of your friends are going to an extravagant party... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245044.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...and you're the only one not invited! And they all know it and look at you with pity in their eyes (that's what I do to people who haven't read the Harry Potter books, hehehe, they deserve it XD). So, naturally, while we were discussing favorite series, the name Kate Daniels will pop out almost instantly and people would start recommending the books, praising them to no end until I was convinced I must've lived in a cave all this time. There was only one thing to do:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245045.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, how do you review one of the most loved and cherished books amongst the Goodreads community? Obviously, words weren't enough, so I did the only thing I'm slightly less crappy at than writing - I drew stuff (cause pictures are supposed to help get points across...somehow?) And the verdict is:<br><br>I thought it was kind of... meh? <br><br>*flies away to another galaxy*<br><br>THE END <br><br>...<br><br>I really really really wanted to LOVE this book, to go crazy about the romance between Kate and Curran, to swoon over the Beast Lord like everybody else, to be completely emerged in this post-apocalyptic world, where magic is real and monsters lurk at every corner. But I didn't. Don't ask why, I can't even explain it myself...well, I CAN, but then 99% of whoever's reading this sad excuse of a review will disagree anyways, so why bother?<br><br>...And because I'm feeling rather suicidal, here is a quick list of what didn't work for me the most:<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>-Undeveloped world-building + nagging feeling of a <i>deja-vu</i> (Mercy Thompson, Anita Blake, Written in Red, Jane Yellowrock, etc.), a city inhabited by shapeshifters, vampires, fairies and so on, doesn't seem that... unordinary or exciting anymore. Nothing to set it apart for me from most other UFs I've read. <br><br>-Protagonist - hilarious, strong and courageous. However, boring, excessively (and needlessly in some cases) violent, never surprised me and the constant self-sacrifice attempts for the greater good (there were at least 3) were just too much for me to care by the end. Didn't feel like a real person to me. <br><br>-Romance - Alpha-male romance worked for me in the Fever series, but that's because it took time to develop. Here, it seemed forced, shallow and too basic. I've been assured it gets better later on. <br><br>-Story - some monster wants to rape Kate, impregnate her and feed her to the baby...this was repeated so many times (by Kate, Curran, bad guy) to the point where it just sounded ridiculous. Kate is also extra special and super powerful. Curran is a pack leader with anger-management issues? Who appointed him in the first place?!? Oh, and there is a human boyfriend-material who wanted to get into Kate's jeans. <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Yep, I'd better run for my life now... XD <br><br>As you can see, yes, I could point out each element that didn't work for me, all the flows that I've noticed and every thing that I found lacking, but, in the end, we don't love a book, because it's perfect. We love it because a part of it resonates with a part of who we are. After all, the version of <i>Magic Bites</i> I saw in my head is completely different and unique from the way each one of us experienced the book to begin with. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245046.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The version I saw wasn't doing it for me - I can blame my lack of imagination, my Urban Fantasy fatigue or my personal annoyance with life in general. So please don't <s>kill</s> hate me... XD <br><br>With all that being said, I'm not giving up on the series. I'll still try the second and probably the third book, and who knows, might be enough to get me hooked. But for now, I'll just have to face the hard truth - I'm not a Kate Daniels fan (yet). I won't get excited when a new book is announced, I won't participate in the buddy reads for the ninth book or scream my heart out whenever someone posts a fanart of Curran. My life will be a never-ending misery...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245047.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442509396i/16245048.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1719124775713444029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_571232385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571232385" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571232385?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571232385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3504885138506723517">I'd been putting this book off for a while because a lot of people compared Kate to Anita Blake and I didn't think I could handle dealing with another emotionally crippled main character, even if she was a bad ass. While I agree that there are a lot of similarities between the two (ass kickery, gross amounts of natural magical talent, smart aleckness) I was pleasantly surprised that Kate didn't come with Anita's pitfalls. Yes there was some boo-hooing and some 'why me' but it happened towards th</span>
  <span id="freeText3504885138506723517" style="display:none">I'd been putting this book off for a while because a lot of people compared Kate to Anita Blake and I didn't think I could handle dealing with another emotionally crippled main character, even if she was a bad ass. While I agree that there are a lot of similarities between the two (ass kickery, gross amounts of natural magical talent, smart aleckness) I was pleasantly surprised that Kate didn't come with Anita's pitfalls. Yes there was some boo-hooing and some 'why me' but it happened towards the end of the book and I felt some of it was warranted. Who wouldn't beat themselves up after their oversight led to more people dying?<br /><br />This book was an easy/quick read with a few holes in it (Why don't combustion engines work when tech falls? What causes these fluctuations in the first place?) but still managed to pull emotional responses from me. I liked it and will continue the series while praying that Kate's vagina doesn't turn into some magical disneyland that all the men in the series line up to get in to (Anita!). <br /><br /><b>This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.thealliterates.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alliterates.</a></b></span>

<div id="review_194889805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194889805" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194889805?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425264201" href="/book/show/15808652-magic-bites">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-read">lib-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194889805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8146631138904744914"><b>Actual rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Well . . . damn. This didn't turn out as I'd planned. While reading this I kept thinking to myself, <i>Just go with three stars, almost everyone else you know has. The series will get better as it goes, just as everyone says, then you can rave and give them four.</i> Although there were plenty things that bothered me about this, there were still more things that I liked. In fact, I would say that this surpassed my expectations.<br/><br/>But let us get the bad stuff out of the way first: I</span>
  <span id="freeText8146631138904744914" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Well . . . damn. This didn't turn out as I'd planned. While reading this I kept thinking to myself, <i>Just go with three stars, almost everyone else you know has. The series will get better as it goes, just as everyone says, then you can rave and give them four.</i> Although there were plenty things that bothered me about this, there were still more things that I liked. In fact, I would say that this surpassed my expectations.<br /><br />But let us get the bad stuff out of the way first: I think my biggest problem was the beginning. All of a sudden you're thrust into this world where vampires are more reptilian/alien-esque Spider-Men than the (supposedly) gorgeous immortal gods we're currently used to (which is rather nice, actually), and there's talk of <i>dhaes</i> and I'm like, what the hell are those? I think there should've been some type of guide in the beginning or a prologue where Kate does an introduction of the world you're about to enter. Like a preparation chapter or something.<br /><br />Even though I was a little leery of her at first, I quickly grew to like Kate. She has one of those personalities that you have to get used to, but once you do she isn't bad. She has spunk and I like how simple she tries to keep her life even in the midst of the chaotic world she lives in. And I think we've only touched the surface when it comes to the magic she can wield.<br /><br />I kept thinking that when Kate met the Beast Lord a.k.a. Curran, he would have a long mane of golden hair — you know, because he's a lion shapechanger — well, if it <i>had</i> turned out that way, that would've undoubtedly been the end for me. Thankfully, that wasn't the case. Curran is described as having blonde hair that is too short to grab. Yahtzee.<br /><br />The romance in this is very light, which is nice when compared to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136266535" rel="nofollow noopener">sex fest</a> I read not long ago. Still, I enjoy a little romance in my reading, so I'm interested to see if anything arises between Kate and <s>Curran</s> one of the men in her life in the next installment. <br />In <i>Magic Bites</i> Kate has a love interest for a short time but things didn't really seem right between them IMO. But there <i>does</i> seem to be some sexual tension (or is that just plain ol' tension?) between Kate and Curran. We shall see what becomes of that.<br /><br />Although this has nothing to do with the book itself, it begs to be mentioned: I hate the cover. It looks like an amateur design effort and the girl looks like an unsuccessful* hooker brandishing a sword. Plus her nose looks as big as the cat's and she's wearing too much makeup to be the always-fuctionally-dressed Kate Daniels. Just an observation.<br /><br />I do see a lot of potential in this series and if the ratings are anything to go by, this series gets better. So I'm quite anxious to begin the reading the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1811543.Magic_Burns__Kate_Daniels___2_" title="Magic Burns (Kate Daniels, #2) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns</a>.<br /><br />*Unsuccessful because there is no man in his right mind who would go near a hooker with a sword. I'm sure you get my meaning.<br /><br />*****************************************************************<br /><br /><b>My reviews of other titles in this series:</b><br /><br />Book #2 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197030282" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Burns</a><br />Book #3 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198478924" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Strikes</a><br />Book #4 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200481479" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bleeds</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8146631138904744914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_589849322" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/589849322" />
    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/589849322?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller?shelf=my-library-catalogue">my-library-catalogue</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589849322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4064230654710720906">I think I have a “read only the first book of every urban fantasy series you come across” problem, and Magic Bites is just one more victim in a long line of my series ADD. My intention is to continue on in all of them eventually, but unfortunately this one is pretty low on that list.<br/><br/>It started out with such a bang, too: a strong female protagonists who totally handles her shit against an ugly vampire (a small, misshapen creature that had me celebrating a grittier take on supernatural beings). It</span>
  <span id="freeText4064230654710720906" style="display:none">I think I have a “read only the first book of every urban fantasy series you come across” problem, and Magic Bites is just one more victim in a long line of my series ADD. My intention is to continue on in all of them eventually, but unfortunately this one is pretty low on that list.<br /><br />It started out with such a bang, too: a strong female protagonists who totally handles her shit against an ugly vampire (a small, misshapen creature that had me celebrating a grittier take on supernatural beings). It even had a compelling mystery to get the story started. These attributes remain in place throughout the novel, so it’s fair to say my disappointment comes down to a specific issue: the development of the love story (or lack thereof).<br /><br />Frankly, for the first half of the book, I wasn’t sure who the love interest was supposed to be, which is just fine with me because the protagonist had a few viable options and I was actually looking forward to seeing how (and if) the sparks would begin to generate. Then, all of a sudden, she was in LOVE with one of them, and I’m over here reeling in my recliner wondering “did I miss something??!” No joke, I flipped back and skimmed the previous few chapters and even checked page numbers to make sure I wasn’t the victim of a misprint. Nope… It really happened that fast.<br /><br />It’s probably because I’ve tried so many urban fantasies that I’ve come to expect strong relationship development within them, even if it’s not the main focus of the story. I also received oodles of positive feedback on this series from customers and fellow bloggers, so I definitely expected more right from the start.<br /><br />Going forward, I have high hopes. I mean, people love these authors for a reason, and there were so many other things that showed promise that I’m willing to give it another go eventually… I just want to delve a little deeper into the other handful of series that hits bullseyes on all accounts first.<br /><br />5/8/17 Update: I've since read beyond the first book, and the series is now in contention to be one of my favorites. It gets waaaaaaayy better! :)<br /><br />Via the Obsessive Bookseller at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.NikiHawkes.com">www.NikiHawkes.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4064230654710720906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410809753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4857146566668061976">Honestly, as long as I'm just focusing on the Urban Fantasy Romance angle of the tale, it's fine, but when it comes right down to all the weres and the types of vamps, it's all pretty much old hat. <br/><br/>So What's really good about the series? The character development. So far it's a pretty solid introduction and the meet-cute is pretty funny. Our MC is kind of a mess with her magic and her sword, but that's okay when the big bad kitty decides he likes her and wants to "help" her.<br/><br/>The vamps do have an </span>
  <span id="freeText4857146566668061976" style="display:none">Honestly, as long as I'm just focusing on the Urban Fantasy Romance angle of the tale, it's fine, but when it comes right down to all the weres and the types of vamps, it's all pretty much old hat. <br /><br />So What's really good about the series? The character development. So far it's a pretty solid introduction and the meet-cute is pretty funny. Our MC is kind of a mess with her magic and her sword, but that's okay when the big bad kitty decides he likes her and wants to "help" her.<br /><br />The vamps do have an interesting twist in species and the whole magic system also has some interesting twists, especially in how all the races tend to mix and match in subtle, almost SF, ways. In fact, I do rather like how the SF features of the world don't play nicely with the magical, and vice-versa. It kinda requires everyone to keep a nice balance going on, but of course that's not really happening with our main couple. It's mostly magic and genes and a lot of power eating. :)<br /><br />No problem. Like I said, a decent introduction. I probably wouldn't have cared enough to continue with the series based on this, alone, but because there's a TON of rave reviews surround this whole series and because I know that UF in general has this problem of slow-starting, I really don't have any problems being patient.<br /><br />It's not like the setup is bad, and I have the benefit of having read a few of the Inkeeper books, so I'm already a fan of the authors. :) Looking forward to reading more!<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103917489" />
    <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela"><img alt="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487543962p2/28640648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103917489?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela">Melissa (Ever So Mela)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425264201" href="/book/show/15808652-magic-bites">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melissa (Ever So Mela) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=strong-leading-lady">strong-leading-lady</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=sarcasm-is-a-gift">sarcasm-is-a-gift</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103917489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4259701782659992195">Well like I said before, this will only be a little rambling because trust me, I have tons of friends who's reviews are a lot more awesome than the one I could come up with right now. <br/><br/>If you follow my reviews you'll likely see I don't tend to read adult UF, like, at all. The last series I did read was the Night Huntress(which I left halfway)...or was it the Fever series(another one I left halfway)?? I'm too lazy to look it up. The thing is, they don't tend to wow me and they are always too freak</span>
  <span id="freeText4259701782659992195" style="display:none">Well like I said before, this will only be a little rambling because trust me, I have tons of friends who's reviews are a lot more awesome than the one I could come up with right now. <br><br>If you follow my reviews you'll likely see I don't tend to read adult UF, like, at all. The last series I did read was the Night Huntress(which I left halfway)...or was it the Fever series(another one I left halfway)?? I'm too lazy to look it up. The thing is, they don't tend to wow me and they are always too freaking loooong. Like seriously <i>why must these series have 8-10 books????</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436739422ra/15497966.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The point to my incessant talking is that I stray. I avoid. I elude. Someone mentions UF, I say, <i>maybe later</i>. And that's the thing. <br><br><b> I think I've been missing out</b><br><br>Well, <u>NO LONGER</u>! I have drank the kool aid that is Kate Daniels. <br><br>Now, I can't say I wholeheartedly love this. That would be a lie. See, I was lost for more than half the story and bored for the other part. I'm pretty sure that has to do with my reading slump but, maybe, it also had to do with the way the story was told. Look, I'm usually one of those readers who doesn't get the mystery until the very end (maybe that's why I hate thrillers/suspense so much) but damn. This book took it to a whole new level. Even after the culprit appeared I thought that maybe it wasn't true. The way they would jump to conclusions or find new leads lost me constantly. The world building was kind of lacking and I mean in the sense of "how does the world go round"? I was constantly speculating as to how things worked and still there are things I have no clue as to what really happened. <br><br>I couldn't be the only one with these questions, right? <br>Like:<br>➞How did magic come to be?<br>➞Are we talking Atlanta, Georgia?<br>➞And if we are, what the heck happened to the world?<br>➞Is it called feylanterns because there are Fey somewhere?<br><br>Another thing is, this is slow. Heinously so. Nothing <i>really</i> happens up until 60% or so. And even when actions is taking place, it reads slow. Does that make sense? <br><br><b>But</b> don't worry cause it wasn't all bad, hence the 3 stars. <br>Personally Kate was enjoyable and she did make me snicker on occasion, though that's a far cry from calling her funny. She had her sarcastic moments and <br>in all honestly I'm quite happy she's a special snowflake. Yes, I just admitted that. <br>Saiman-hopefully I'm writing it right- is still my fav character for some reason, even though we rarely see him. <br>As to Curran, screw you <i>Your Majesty</i>. He's a domineering butthole of a cat. lol this is supposed to be the pros. Oh well. <br>Also kudos on the vampires. No shimmery ones here. <br><br><br><b>What a messy review, right?</b><br>Well, I did promise rambling and what am I if not a woman of my word. <br><br>Here are some better reviews: <br>➩<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715402388?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a> Thanks for the rec &lt;3<br>➩<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/804194919?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Shandra</a><br>➩<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955445720?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a> and her crustaceans<br>➩<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1049969551?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Teryna90</a><br>➩<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/902468361?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookaholic</a><br>➩<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130214303?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Lizet</a><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421940798i/13432097.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alas, I will be continuing cause I have to fall for Curran (duh) and Kate is vulgar. Me likey.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1542087104?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1542087104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17102418582044672051">Oh, well. What do they say? <i>About damn time</i>.<br/><br/><b>3.5<br/><br/>"The day I needed an escort was the day I'd turn my saber over to someone who knew what to do with it."</b><br/><br/>I promise I'll be short and straight to the point, but, first, an applause to me, because I have finally joined the hype. Yay!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451938092ra/17623743.gif' width='420' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And now, let's see what we have.<br/><br/>•<i>Magic Bites</i> is, glaringly, a book with an <b>introductory</b> function. I would be perfectly fine with this if the purpose of being introductory was fulfilled, which, with my greatest disappointment</span>
  <span id="freeText17102418582044672051" style="display:none">Oh, well. What do they say? <i>About damn time</i>.<br><br><b>3.5<br><br>"The day I needed an escort was the day I'd turn my saber over to someone who knew what to do with it."</b><br><br>I promise I'll be short and straight to the point, but, first, an applause to me, because I have finally joined the hype. Yay!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451938092ra/17623743.gif" width="420" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now, let's see what we have.<br><br>•<i>Magic Bites</i> is, glaringly, a book with an <b>introductory</b> function. I would be perfectly fine with this if the purpose of being introductory was fulfilled, which, with my greatest disappointment, it wasn't. I didn't think I could ever say something like this, but this book brought me to the point of craving an info-dump:<b> important notions</b> regarding the world Kate and the other characters move in <b>are taken for granted</b>, leaving the readers at their guess, other things are only hinted, the most disparate pieces of information are provided here and here forming a larger picture with too little order in it to seem uniform and consistent. I often felt more confused than anything, actually. But then again, this world also contain a <b>great variety</b> of elements that looks incredibly promising for the future, if paired with more definition and attention to the details.<br><br>•I had some problem with the <b>pace</b>. This book made something happen to me that I'm a bit ashamed of: it made me fall asleep. I <i>never</i> fall asleep while I'm reading. If I'm tired or the book does no hold my attention anymore, I reach the end of the paragraph, close the book and go to bed. Here I fell asleep with the blasted thing still open. And I wasn't even particularly tired.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455065668ra/18050193.gif" width="420" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But beware, it's not that the book is boring. It just feels annoyingly <b>repetitive</b> and <b>unoriginal</b> at times, and more than once I found myself wondering why I was still reading. But the thing is, <b>I kept reading nonetheless</b>. That must mean something.<br><br>•That must mean something, and I can also point out why: first of all, the <b>interactions</b> between the characters are often <b>funny</b> and always <b>natural</b> and <b>spontaneous</b>, also because the <b>cast</b> is pretty interesting, and I adore how the Andrews write their main characters.<br><br>•On second thought, <b>I adore how the Andrews write, period</b>.<br><br>•<b>Kate</b>, the main character, is <b>wonderful</b>. Any other adjective would be superfluous, but I have never been a girl of few words and have no intention to become one anytime soon, so: you know when a ya fantasy/sci-fi book promise you a kick-ass heroine, right? And you duly find yourself stuck with an insufferable brat that make you want to be able to sneak into the book just to punch her in the face?<br>Well, people, the dark days are over.<b> Kick-ass heroine 2.0 has been delivered, with a sharp tongue and witty retorts to boot</b>. <br><br>Enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17102418582044672051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <u>Fifth re-read: 16.07.19</u>
</b><br/>I just had to re-read this book (maybe series, we'll see) again after reading <b>
  <i>Mercy Thompson</i>
